## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / dynamical systems for concentration)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a chemical concentration A, which is the standard object modeled by kinetic rate laws (ODEs). With only t and A available, the most likely relationships are order-based kinetics, reversible relaxation toward an equilibrium concentration, or externally driven/time-varying rate coefficients.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay/production: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption/formation under saturation or constant flux)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive-like kinetics, pseudo-first-order conditions)
- First-order with source (inflow/formation): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (continuous production plus first-order loss; chemostat/well-mixed feed-loss approximation)
- Relaxation to equilibrium (linear): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady-state/equilibrium concentration c1)
- Second-order decay (self-reaction): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular 2A -> products under mass-action)
- General nth-order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical or effective reaction order not necessarily integer)
- Autocatalytic growth with depletion (logistic-type kinetics in A): dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (autocatalysis with carrying-capacity-like limitation from finite substrate)
- Inhibition-like denominator (self-inhibition/limited capacity): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate saturates with A due to capacity limits or mixed control)
- Reversible approach with nonlinear forward term: dA_dt = -c0 * (A**c1 - c2) (net rate as difference between a nonlinear forward dependence and an equilibrium term)
- Time-varying first-order rate (exponential ramp): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (changing conditions over time: temperature program, catalyst activation/deactivation, illumination changes)
- Time-varying first-order rate (power-law in time): dA_dt = -c0 * t**c1 * A (aging, diffusion-controlled effective rate, or empirical nonstationary kinetics)
- Driven/periodic forcing (e.g., modulated input): dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (periodic feed/irradiation leading to oscillatory forcing)
- Stretched-exponential-like effective kinetics (time-dependent prefactor): dA_dt = -c0 * t**(c1 - 1) * A (appears when A follows exp(-c * t**c1) in heterogeneous/complex media)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is proportional to A (straight line through origin when plotting dA_dt vs A), favor first-order forms: dA_dt ≈ -c * A.
- If dA_dt is approximately constant over wide A ranges, favor zero-order: dA_dt ≈ -c.
- If -dA_dt grows faster than linearly with A (curvature upward in -dA_dt vs A), consider higher-order/power-law: -dA_dt ∝ A**n with n>1.
- If dA_dt changes sign at a nonzero A (stable fixed point), model relaxation toward equilibrium: dA_dt ∝ -(A - A_eq) or nonlinear variants with a root at A_eq.
- If dA_dt depends on t even at fixed A (non-overlapping dA_dt vs A curves across time), include explicit time-varying rate coefficients like exp(c*t) or t**c.
- If the rate magnitude saturates at large A (|dA_dt| plateaus), use rational forms like A/(A+c) to encode capacity/transport limitation.
- If dynamics show initial acceleration (more negative or more positive dA_dt as A increases from small values) then later slowdown near a ceiling, consider autocatalytic-with-limitation structures A*(A_max-A).
- If there is oscillatory structure in residuals vs t after fitting a simple rate law, include a sinusoidal forcing term in t to represent periodic driving.

Best expression     : A**2*c0 + A*c1 + c2*sin(c3*log(c4*exp(c5*Abs(A)) + 1) + c6)
Structure desc      : Quadratic in A plus a nested nonlinear sinusoid whose phase is a log of an exp in |A| (sin(c3*log(1+c4*exp(c5|A|))+c6)). A enters in A^2 and through |A| inside exp→log→sin; t absent. With c1≈-7.7e-3 ~ 0, the linear term is negligible; c3=0.069 is small so the phase changes slowly despite exp growth, leaving an oscillation of amplitude 4.334 around a near-pure quadratic baseline c0=-0.774. Approximate simplification: y≈-0.774 A^2+4.334*sin(0.069*log(1+3.696*exp(3.365|A|))+2.863).

============================================================

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK1)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A**c1 - c2*A + c3*_w*cos(log(A + c4))
Candidate formulas: 78

GT is the fixed function of \(A\):
\[
f(A)= -0.7725880991\,A^2\;-\;0.7725880991\,A\;+\;0.7402077580\cos(\log(A+1)).
\]
So any matching candidate must be able (possibly under a domain restriction like \(A\ge 0\) or \(A>-1\)) to produce:
- a quadratic term in \(A^2\) with coefficient \(-0.7725880991\),
- a linear term in \(A\) with coefficient \(-0.7725880991\),
- plus a cosine of \(\log(A+1)\) with amplitude \(0.7402077580\),
- and **no other functional dependence** (no extra logs, rationals, exponentials, \(t\)-dependence, etc.).

Also note: candidates use \(\sin(\cdot)\) a lot; \(\sin(x+\phi)\) can equal \(\cos(x)\) by choosing \(\phi=\pi/2\). But the *inside* must still be exactly \(\log(A+1)\) (up to an additive constant), not \(\log(|A|+1)\), not \(\log(\exp(|A|)+1)\), etc., unless a domain restriction makes them identical.

---

### 1. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + c2\sin(c3\log(c4e^{c5|A|}+1)+c6)\)
Polynomial part can match by \(c0=c1=-0.772588...\). Trig part: needs \(\sin(\,\log(A+1)+\text{phase})\). But argument is \(\log(c4e^{c5|A|}+1)\), not \(\log(A+1)\). No constant choice makes \(c4e^{c5|A|}+1 \equiv A+1\) on any continuous domain (it’s exponential in \(|A|\)). **No.**

### 2. \(Ac0 + A^{c1}c2/(A^{c1}+c3) + c4\sin(Ac5+c6)\)
Has \(\sin(\text{linear in }A)\), not \(\cos(\log(A+1))\). Rational term can’t become \(-0.7726A^2\) globally on an interval. **No.**

### 3. \(Ac0 + A^{c1}c2\log(c3|A|+1) + c4\sin(Ac5+c6)\)
Trig wrong (linear in \(A\)). Also has \(A^{c1}\log(\cdot)\) not present in GT. **No.**

### 4. \(Ac0 + c1\sin(Ac2+c3) + c4 t/(Ac5+c6) + c7/(Ac5+c6)\)
Contains \(t\) unless \(c4=0\). Still has rational-in-\(A\) term and \(\sin(\text{linear }A)\). **No.**

### 5. \(Ac0 + Ac1\log(c2|A|+1) + c3\sin(Ac4+c5)\)
Wrong functional forms. **No.**

### 6. \(Ac0 + c1\sin(Ac2+c3) + c4\log(Ac5+1)\)
No \(A^2\) term; trig is \(\sin(\text{linear }A)\). **No.**

### 7. Big expression all divided by \((Ac1+c2)\) with \(\sin(Ac5+c6)\)
Overall rational structure; cannot equal a polynomial plus \(\cos(\log(A+1))\) on an interval unless denominator is constant, but denominator is \(Ac1+c2\) (can’t be constant for varying \(A\) unless \(c1=0\), then it’s constant \(c2\)). If \(c1=0\), expression becomes a linear combination of \(A^2,A,\sin(A\cdot)\),constant — still trig is \(\sin(\text{linear }A)\), not \(\cos(\log(A+1))\). **No.**

### 8. \(Ac0 + A c1/(Ac2+c3) + c4\sin(Ac5+c6) + c7/(Ac2+c3)\)
Trig wrong; rational terms not in GT. **No.**

### 9. \(c0|A|^{c1} + c2\sin(c3\log(c4|A|+1)+c5) + c6\log(Ac7+1)\)
Could set \(c6=0\). Then need \(|A|^{c1}\) to produce both \(-0.7726A^2\) and \(-0.7726A\): impossible (single power term can’t give both). Also trig uses \(\log(c4|A|+1)\); even with \(A\ge 0\) and \(c4=1\) it becomes \(\log(A+1)\), good, and phase can convert sin to cos. But polynomial part still can’t match both \(A^2\) and \(A\). **No.**

### 10. Rational in \(|\sqrt A|\)
Requires \(A\ge 0\). Still yields rational functions in \(\sqrt A\), not polynomial + cosine(log). **No.**

### 11. \(A c0/(A+c1) + c2 + c3|A|^2 + c4/(Ac5+c6)\)
No cosine(log). Extra rational terms. **No.**

### 12. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + c2 + c3\log(\,| \sin(\cdots \log(|A|+1)\cdots)|+1)\)
Has nested log/sin and \(t\). Not reducible to \(\cos(\log(A+1))\). **No.**

### 13. \(Ac0 + c1\sin(Ac2+c3) + c4\sin(c5\log(c6e^{Ac7}+1)+c8)\)
Second sine has \(\log(c6e^{Ac7}+1)\), not \(\log(A+1)\). First sine is \(\sin(\text{linear }A)\). Also no \(A^2\) term. **No.**

### 14. \(Ac0 + A c1|A| + c2\sin(c3\log(c4|A|+1)+c5)\)
On domain \(A\ge 0\), \(A|A|=A^2\). Great: polynomial part can match by setting \(c1=-0.772588...\) and \(c0=-0.772588...\).
Trig part: on \(A\ge 0\), \(\log(c4|A|+1)=\log(c4A+1)\). To match \(\cos(\log(A+1))\), we need \(c4=1\) so inside is \(\log(A+1)\). Then choose \(c3=1\) and phase \(c5=\pi/2\) so \(\sin(\log(A+1)+\pi/2)=\cos(\log(A+1))\). Finally set \(c2=0.7402077580\).
This matches GT exactly on the plausible continuous domain \(A\ge 0\) (also requires \(A>-1\) for log; \(A\ge 0\) satisfies). **YES, match.**

### 15. \(Ac0 + c1\sin(Ac2+c3) + c4e^{Ac5}\)

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the GT:

**GT:** `-0.7726*A² - 0.7726*A + 0.7402*cos(log(A + 1))`

Key structural components of GT:
1. A quadratic term: `-0.7726*A²`
2. A linear term: `-0.7726*A`
3. A trigonometric term: `0.7402*cos(log(A + 1))`

Note: `cos(log(A+1))` can be written as `sin(log(A+1) + π/2)`.

For A ≥ 0, `|A| = A`, `|sqrt(A)| = sqrt(A)`, etc.

Let me analyze each candidate systematically.

**Candidate 1:** `A²*c0 + A*c1 + c2*sin(c3*log(c4*exp(c5*|A|) + 1) + c6)`

For this to match GT, we need `sin(c3*log(c4*exp(c5*A) + 1) + c6) = cos(log(A+1))`. Setting c5=0: `c4*exp(0)+1 = c4+1`, so `sin(c3*log(c4+1) + c6)` = constant. That doesn't work. We need the argument to be `log(A+1)`. If c4=1, c5→0... but `exp(c5*A)` with c5=0 gives constant. We can't get `log(A+1)` from `log(c4*exp(c5*A)+1)` for all A. These are structurally different functions.
